# [Kubernetes] Client-Go Package Documentation

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes
**Difficulty:** HARD
**Category:** package-documentation
**Task Type:** Documentation Generation - Code Inference

## Description

Generate comprehensive package documentation (`doc.go`) for the `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go` package in Kubernetes. This is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. The existing documentation has been stripped from the workspace. You must infer the documentation entirely from the source code.

**Why this requires cross-package context:** client-go is a top-level library that integrates 6+ sub-packages (kubernetes, dynamic, discovery, rest, tools/cache, tools/clientcmd). Understanding its full scope requires exploring how these sub-packages interact, what patterns they enable (informers, listers, workqueues), and how they connect to the API server. Sourcegraph search provides this cross-package context efficiently.

## Task

YOU MUST CREATE A `doc.go` FILE at `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/doc.go`.

### Requirements

Your `doc.go` file should:

1. **Package Overview**: Explain the purpose of client-go as the official Go client for the Kubernetes API
2. **Key Packages**: Document the major sub-packages and their roles:
   - `kubernetes` (typed Clientset)
   - `dynamic` (dynamic client for CRDs)
   - `discovery` (API group/version discovery)
   - `tools/cache` (informers, listers, controller pattern)
   - `tools/clientcmd` (kubeconfig loading)
   - `rest` (lower-level REST client)
3. **Connecting to the API**: Describe in-cluster vs out-of-cluster configuration
4. **Interacting with API Objects**: Cover typed vs dynamic clients, CRDs, Server-Side Apply
5. **Building Controllers**: Explain the informer/lister/workqueue pattern and leader election

### Go Documentation Conventions

- Use `// Package clientgo ...` line comment style OR `/* ... */` block comment style
- Include copyright header (Apache 2.0, The Kubernetes Authors)
- Use `# Heading` syntax within doc comments for sections (Go 1.19+ doc links)
- Reference sub-packages with their import paths
- Keep descriptions precise and technically accurate

### Kubernetes Documentation Style

- Be concise but comprehensive — cover the "what" and "why", not implementation details
- Use bullet lists for enumerating sub-packages and their purposes
- Reference related packages by their full import paths
- Include practical guidance (when to use typed vs dynamic clients, in-cluster vs out-of-cluster)

### Key Files to Examine

- `kubernetes/clientset.go` — Typed Clientset
- `dynamic/interface.go` — Dynamic client interface
- `discovery/discovery_client.go` — Discovery client
- `rest/config.go` — REST client configuration
- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go` — Informer framework
- `tools/clientcmd/client_config.go` — Kubeconfig loading
- `applyconfigurations/` — Server-Side Apply support

### Format

The output must be a valid Go `doc.go` file following Kubernetes conventions:

```go
/*
Copyright YEAR The Kubernetes Authors.

Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
...
*/

// Package clientgo ...
package clientgo
```

## Success Criteria

- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/doc.go` file exists
- Contains valid Go package documentation
- Accurately describes client-go's purpose and key sub-packages
- Covers connecting to the API, interacting with objects, and building controllers
- Follows Go and Kubernetes documentation conventions

## Testing

The verifier checks that `doc.go` was created and scores it based on:
- File existence and valid Go package declaration
- Coverage of key sub-packages (kubernetes, dynamic, discovery, tools/cache, rest)
- Mentions of configuration patterns (in-cluster, kubeconfig)
- References to controller pattern concepts (informers, listers, workqueues)

**Time Limit:** 15 minutes

\n463: // Discovery retrieves the DiscoveryClient\n464: func (c *Clientset) Discovery() discovery.DiscoveryInterface {\n465: \tif c == nil {\n466: \t\treturn nil\n467: \t}\n468: \treturn c.DiscoveryClient\n469: }\n470: \n471: // NewForConfig creates a new Clientset for the given config.\n472: // If config's RateLimiter is not set and QPS and Burst are acceptable,\n473: // NewForConfig will generate a rate-limiter in configShallowCopy.\n474: // NewForConfig is equivalent to NewForConfigAndClient(c, httpClient),\n475: // where httpClient was generated with rest.HTTPClientFor(c).\n476: func NewForConfig(c *rest.Config) (*Clientset, error) {\n477: \tconfigShallowCopy := *c\n478: \n479: \tif configShallowCopy.UserAgent == \"\" {\n480: \t\tconfigShallowCopy.UserAgent = rest.DefaultKubernetesUserAgent()\n481: \t}\n482: \n483: \t// share the transport between all clients\n484: \thttpClient, err := rest.HTTPClientFor(&configShallowCopy)\n485: \tif err != nil {\n486: \t\treturn nil, err\n487: \t}\n488: \n489: \treturn NewForConfigAndClient(&configShallowCopy, httpClient)\n490: }\n491: \n492: // NewForConfigAndClient creates a new Clientset for the given config and http client.\n493: // Note the http client provided takes precedence over the configured transport values.\n494: // If config's RateLimiter is not set and QPS and Burst are acceptable,\n495: // NewForConfigAndClient will generate a rate-limiter in configShallowCopy.\n496: func NewForConfigAndClient(c *rest.Config, httpClient *http.Client) (*Clientset, error) {\n497: \tconfigShallowCopy := *c\n498: \tif configShallowCopy.RateLimiter == nil && configShallowCopy.QPS > 0 {\n499: \t\tif configShallowCopy.Burst <= 0 {\n500: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"burst is required to be greater than 0 when RateLimiter is not set and QPS is set to greater than 0\")\n501: \t\t}\n502: \t\tconfigShallowCopy.RateLimiter = flowcontrol.NewTokenBucketRateLimiter(configShallowCopy.QPS, configShallowCopy.Burst)\n503: \t}\n504: \n505: \tvar cs Clientset\n506: \tvar err error\n507: \tcs.admissionregistrationV1, err = An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n44: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n45: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n46: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n47: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n48: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n49: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n50: //\\n51: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n52: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n53: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n54: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n55: //\\n56: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n57: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n58: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n59: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n60: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n61: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n62: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n63: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n64: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n65: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n66: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n67: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n68: // selector.\\n69: //\\n70: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n71: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n72: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n73: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n74: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n75: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n76: //\\n77: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n78: // during `Run()`.\\n79: //\\n80: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n81: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n82: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n83: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n84: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n85: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n86: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n87: //\\n88: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n89: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n90: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n91: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n92: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n93: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n94: //\\n95: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n96: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n97: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n98: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n99: // into its constituent parts.\\n100: //\\n101: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n102: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n103: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n104: //\\n105: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n106: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n107: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n108: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n109: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n110: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n111: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n112: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n113: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n114: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n115: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n116: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n117: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n118: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n119: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n120: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n121: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n122: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n123: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n124: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n125: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n126: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n127: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n128: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n129: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n130: //\\n131: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n132: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n133: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n134: // to something else, for example through a\\n135: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n136: //\\n137: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n138: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n139: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n140: type SharedInformer interface {\\n141: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n142: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n143: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n144: \\t// different handlers.\\n145: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n146: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n147: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n148: \\t//\\n149: \\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\\n150: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n151: \\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\\n152: \\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\\n153: \\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\\n154: \\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\\n155: \\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\\n156: \\t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\\n157: \\t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\\n158: \\t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\\n159: \\t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\\n160: \\t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\\n161: \\t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\\n162: \\t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\\n163: \\t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\\n164: \\t// be competing load \\tresyncNeeded := false\\n946: \\tnow := p.clock.Now()\\n947: \\tfor listener := range p.listeners {\\n948: \\t\\t// need to loop through all the listeners to see if they need to resync so we can *sharedProcessor) resyncCheckPeriodChanged(logger klog.Logger, resyncCheckPeriod time.Duration) {\\n962: \\tp.listenersLock.RLock()\\n963: \\tdefer p.listenersLock.RUnlock()\\n964: \\n965: \\tfor \\t\\tlistener.setResyncPeriod(resyncPeriod)\\n969: \\t}\\n970: }\\n971: \\n972: // processorListener relays notifications from a sharedProcessor to\\n973: // one ResourceEventHandler --- using two goroutines, two unbuffered\\n974: // channels, and an unbounded ring buffer.  The `add(notification)`\\n975: // function sends the given notification to `addCh`.  One goroutine\\n976: // runs `pop()`, which pumps notifications from `addCh` to `nextCh`\\n977: // using storage in the ring buffer while `nextCh` is not keeping up.\\n978: // Another goroutine runs `run()`, which receives notifications from\\n979: // `nextCh` and synchronously invokes the appropriate handler method.\\n980: //\\n981: // processorListener also keeps track of the adjusted requested resync\\n982: // period of the listener.\\n983: type processorListener struct {\\n984: \\tlogger klog.Logger\\n985: \\tnextCh chan interface{}\\n986: \\taddCh  chan interface{}\\n987: \\n988: \\thandler ResourceEventHandler\\n989: \\n990: \\tsyncTracker *synctrack.SingleFileTracker\\n991: \\n992: \\t// pendingNotifications is an unbounded ring buffer that holds all notifications not yet distributed.\\n993: \\t// There is one per listener, but a failing/stalled listener will have infinite pendingNotifications\\n994: \\t// added until we OOM.\\n995: \\t// TODO: This is no worse than before, since reflectors were backed by unbounded DeltaFIFOs, but\\n996: \\t// we should try to do something better.\\n997: \\tpendingNotifications buffer.RingGrowing\\n998: \\n999: \\t// requestedResyncPeriod is how frequently the listener wants a\\n1000: \\t// full resync from the shared informer, but modified by two\\n1001: \\t// adjustments.  One is imposing a lower bound,\\n1002: \\t// `minimumResyncPeriod`.  The other is another lower bound, the\\n1003: \\t// sharedIndexInformer's `resyncCheckPeriod`, that is imposed (a) only\\n1004: \\t// in AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod invocations made after the\\n1005: \\t// sharedIndexInformer starts and (b) only if the informer does\\n1006: \\t// resyncs at all.\\n1007: \\trequestedResyncPeriod time.Duration\\n1008: \\t// resyncPeriod is the threshold that will be used in the logic\\n1009: \\t// for this listener.  This value differs from\\n1010: \\t// requestedResyncPeriod only when the sharedIndexInformer does\\n1011: \\t// not do resyncs, in which case the value here is zero.  The\\n1012: \\t// actual time between resyncs depends on when the\\n1013: \\t// sharedProcessor's `shouldResync` function is invoked and when\\n1014: \\t// the sharedIndexInformer processes `Sync` type Delta objects.\\n1015: \\tresyncPeriod time.Duration\\n1016: \\t// nextResync is the earliest time the listener should get a full resync\\n1017: \\tnextResync time.Time\\n1018: \\t// resyncLock guards access to resyncPeriod and nextResync\\n1019: \\tresyncLock sync.Mutex\\n1020: }\\n1021: \\n1022: // HasSynced returns true if the source informer has synced, and all\\n1023: // corresponding events have been delivered.\\n1024: func (p *processorListener) HasSynced() bool {\\n1025: \\treturn p.syncTracker.HasSynced()\\n1026: }\\n1027: \\n1028: func newProcessListener(logger klog.Logger, handler ResourceEventHandler, requestedResyncPeriod, resyncPeriod time.Duration, now time.Time, bufferSize int, hasSynced func() bool) *processorListener {\\n1029: \\tret := &processorListener{\\n1030: \\t\\tlogger:                logger,\\n1031: \\t\\tnextCh:                make(chan interface{}),\\n1032: \\t\\taddCh:                 make(chan interface{}),\\n1033: \\t\\thandler:               handler,\\n1034: \\t\\tsyncTracker:           &synctrack.SingleFileTracker{UpstreamHasSynced: hasSynced},\\n1035: \\t\\tpendingNotifications:  *buffer.NewRingGrowing(bufferSize),\\n1036: \\t\\trequestedResyncPeriod: requestedResyncPeriod,\\n1037: \\t\\tresyncPeriod:          resyncPeriod,\\n1038: \\t}\\n1039: \\n1040: \\tret.determineNextResync(now)\\n1041: \\n1042: \\treturn ret\\n1043: }\\n1044: \\n1045: func (p *processorListener) add(notification interface{}) {\\n1046: \\tif a, ok := notification.(addNotification); ok && a.isInInitialList {\\n1047: \\t\\tp.syncTracker.Start()\\n1048: \\t}\\n1049: \\tp.addCh <- notification\\n1050: }\\n1051: \\n1052: func (p *processorListener) pop() {\\n1053: \\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrashWithLogger(p.logger)\\n1054: \\tdefer close(p.nextCh) // Tell .run() to stop\\n1055: \\n1056: \\tvar nextCh chan<- interface{}\\n1057: \\tvar notification interface{}\\n1058: \\tfor {\\n1059: \\t\\tselect {\\n1060: \\t\\tcase nextCh <- notification:\\n1061: \\t\\t\\t// Notification dispatched\\n1062: \\t\\t\\tvar ok bool\\n1063: \\t\\t\\tnotification, ok = p.pendingNotifications.ReadOne()\\n1064: \\t\\t\\tif !ok { // Nothing to pop\\n1065: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextCh = nil // Disable this select case\\n1066: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1067: \\t\\tcase notificationToAdd, ok := <-p.addCh:\\n1068: \\t\\t\\tif !ok {\\n1069: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n1070: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1071: \\t\\t\\tif notification == nil { // No notification to pop (and pendingNotifications is empty)\\n1072: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Optimize the case - skip adding to pendingNotifications\\n1073: \\t\\t\\t\\tnotification = notificationToAdd\\n1074: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextCh = p.nextCh\\n1075: \\t\\t\\t} else { // There is already a notification waiting to be dispatched\\n1076: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.pendingNotifications.WriteOne(notificationToAdd)\\n1077: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1078: \\t\\t}\\n1079: \\t}\\n1080: }\\n1081: \\n1082: func (p *processorListener) run() {\\n1083: \\t// this call blocks until the channel is closed.  When a panic happens during the notification\\n1084: \\t// we will catch it, **the offending item will be skipped!**, and after a short delay (one second)\\n1085: \\t// the next notification will be attempted. This is usually better than the alternative of never\\n1086: \\t// delivering again.\\n1087: \\t//\\n1088: \\t// This only applies if utilruntime is configured to not panic, which is not the default.\\n1089: \\tsleepAfterCrash := false\\n1090: \\tfor next := range p.nextCh {\\n1091: \\t\\tif sleepAfterCrash {\\n1092: \\t\\t\\t// Sleep before processing the next item.\\n1093: \\t\\t\\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\\n1094: \\t\\t}\\n1095: \\t\\tfunc() {\\n1096: \\t\\t\\t// Gets reset below, but only if we get that far.\\n1097: \\t\\t\\tsleepAfterCrash = true\\n1098: \\t\\t\\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrashWithLogger(p.logger)\\n1099: \\n1100: \\t\\t\\tswitch notification := next.(type) {\\n1101: \\t\\t\\tcase updateNotification:\\n1102: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.handler.OnUpdate(notification.oldObj, notification.newObj)\\n1103: \\t\\t\\tcase addNotification:\\n1104: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.handler.OnAdd(notification.newObj, notification.isInInitialList)\\n1105: \\t\\t\\t\\tif notification.isInInitialList {\\n1106: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tp.syncTracker.Finished()\\n1107: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1108: \\t\\t\\tcase deleteNotification:\\n1109: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.handler.OnDelete(notification.oldObj)\\n1110: \\t\\t\\tdefault:\\n1111: \\t\\t\\t\\tutilruntime.HandleErrorWithLogger(p.logger, nil, \\\"unrecognized notification\\\", \\\"notificationType\\\", fmt.Sprintf(\\\"%T\\\", next))\\n1112: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1113: \\t\\t\\tsleepAfterCrash = false\\n1114: \\t\\t}()\\n1115: \\t}\\n1116: }\\n1117: \\n1118: // shouldResync determines if the listener needs a resync. If the listener's resyncPeriod is 0,\\n1119: // this always returns false.\\n1120: func (p *processorListener) shouldResync(now time.Time) bool {\\n1121: \\tp.resyncLock.Lock()\\n1122: \\tdefer p.resyncLock.Unlock()\\n1123: \\n1124: \\tif p.resyncPeriod == 0 {\\n1125: \\t\\treturn false\\n1126: \\t}\\n1127: \\n1128: \\treturn now.After(p.nextResync) || now.Equal(p.nextResync)\\n1129: }\\n1130: \\n1131: func (p *processorListener) determineNextResync(now time.Time) {\\n1132: \\tp.resyncLock.Lock()\\n1133: \\tdefer p.resyncLock.Unlock()\\n1134: \\n1135: \\tp.nextResync = now.Add(p.resyncPeriod)\\n1136: }\\n1137: \\n1138: func (p *processorListener) setResyncPeriod(resyncPeriod time.Duration) {\\n1139: \\tp.resyncLock.Lock()\\n1140: \\tdefer p.resyncLock.Unlock()\\n1141: \\n1142: \\tp.resyncPeriod = resyncPeriod\\n1143: }\\n1144: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go\"}",

    "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package cache\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"context\"\n21: \t\"errors\"\n22: \t\"fmt\"\n23: \t\"sync\"\n24: \t\"sync/atomic\"\n25: \t\"time\"\n26: \n27: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n28: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n29: \tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n30: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n31: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\"\n32: \t\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\"\n33: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n34: \t\"k8s.io/utils/ptr\"\n35: \n36: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n37: \n38: \tclientgofeaturegate \"k8s.io/client-go/features\"\n39: )\n40: \n41: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\n42: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\n43: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n44: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n45: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n46: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n47: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n48: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n49: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n50: //\n51: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n52: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n53: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n54: // other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n55: //\n56: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n57: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n58: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n59: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n60: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n61: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n62: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n63: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n64: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n65: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n66: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n67: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n68: // selector.\n69: //\n70: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n71: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n72: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n73: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n74: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n75: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\n76: //\n77: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n78: // during `Run()`.\n79: //\n80: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n81: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n82: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n83: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n84: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n85: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\n86: // persistently thwart achievement).\n87: //\n88: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n89: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n90: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n91: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n92: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n93: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n94: //\n95: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n96: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n97: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n98: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n99: // into its constituent parts.\n100: //\n101: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n102: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n103: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n104: //\n105: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n106: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n107: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n108: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n109: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n110: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n111: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n112: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n113: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n114: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n115: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n116: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n117: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n118: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n119: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n120: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n121: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n122: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n123: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n124: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n125: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n126: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n127: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n128: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n129: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n130: //\n131: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n132: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n133: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n134: // to something else, for example through a\n135: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n136: //\n137: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n138: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n139: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n140: type SharedInformer interface {\n141: \t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n142: \t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n143: \t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n144: \t// different handlers.\n145: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n146: \t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n147: \t// seen every item in the initial list).\n148: \t//\n149: \t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n150: \tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n151: \t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n152: \t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n153: \t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n154: \t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n155: \t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\n156: \t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\n157: \t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\n158: \t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\n159: \t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\n160: \t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\n161: \t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\n162: \t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\n163: \t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\n164: \t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\n165: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\n166: \t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\n167: \t//\n168: \t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod where\n171: \t// all optional parameters are passed in a struct.\n172: \tAddEventHandlerWithOptions(handler ResourceEventHandler, options HandlerOptions) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n173: \t// RemoveEventHandler removes a formerly added event handler given by\n174: \t// its registration handle.\n175: \t// This function is guaranteed to be idempotent, and thread-safe.\n176: \tRemoveEventHandler(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error\n177: \t// GetStore returns the informer's local cache as a Store.\n178: \tGetStore() Store\n179: context.Context)\n189: \t// HasSynced returns true if the shared informer's store has been\n190: \t// informed by at least one full LIST of the authoritative state\n191: \t// of the informer's object collection.  This is unrelated to \"resync\".\n192: \t//\n193: \t// Note that this doesn't tell you if an individual handler is synced!!\n194: \t// For that, please call HasSynced on the handle returned by\n195: \t// AddEventHandler.\n196: \tHasSynced() bool\n197: \t// LastSyncResourceVersion is the resource version observed when last synced with the underlying\n198: \t// store. The value returned is not synchronized with access to the underlying store and is not\n199: \t// thread-safe.\n200: \tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n201: \n202: \t// The WatchErrorHandler is called whenever ListAndWatch drops the\n203: \t// connection with an error. After calling this handler, the informer\n204: \t// will backoff and retry.\n205: \t//\n206: \t// The default implementation looks at the error type and tries to log\n207: \t// the error message at an appropriate level.\n208: \t//\n209: \t// There's only one handler, so if you call this multiple times, last one\n210: \t// wins; calling after the informer has been started returns an error.\n211: \t//\n212: \t// The handler is intended for visibility, not to e.g. pause the consumers.\n213: \t// The handler should return quickly - any expensive processing should be\n214: \t// offloaded.\n215: \t//\n216: \t// Contextual logging: SetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext should be used instead of SetWatchErrorHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n217: \tSetWatchErrorHandler(handler WatchErrorHandler) error\n218: \n219: \t// SetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext is a variant of SetWatchErrorHandler where\n220: \t// the handler is passed an additional context parameter.\n221: \tSetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext(handler WatchErrorHandlerWithContext) error\n222: \n223: \t// The TransformFunc is called for each object which is about to be stored.\n224: \t//\n225: \t// This function is intended for you to take the opportunity to\n226: \t// remove, transform, or normalize fields. One use case is to strip unused\n227: \t// metadata fields out of objects to save on RAM cost.\n228: \t//\n229: \t// Must be set before starting the informer.\n230: \t//\n231: \t// Please see the comment on TransformFunc for more details.\n232: \tSetTransform(handler TransformFunc) error\n233: \n234: \t// IsStopped reports whether the informer has already been stopped.\n235: \t// Adding event handlers to already stopped informers is not possible.\n236: \t// An informer already stopped will never be started again.\n237: \tIsStopped() bool\n238: }\n239: \n240: // Opaque interface representing the registration of ResourceEventHandler for\n241: // a SharedInformer. Such an informer's resync\n298: // checking period is established when the informer starts running,\n299: // and is the maximum of (a) the minimum of the resync periods\n300: // requested before the informer starts and the\n301: // options.ResyncPeriod given here and (b) the constant\n302: // `minimumResyncPeriod` defined in this file.\n303: func NewSharedIndexInformerWithOptions(lw ListerWatcher, exampleObject runtime.Object, options SharedIndexInformerOptions) SharedIndexInformer {\n304: \trealClock := &clock.RealClock{}\n305: \n306: \tprocessor := &sharedProcessor{clock: realClock}\n307: \tprocessor.listenersRCond = sync.NewCond(processor.listenersLock.RLocker())\n308: \n309: \treturn &sharedIndexInformer{\n310: \t\tindexer:                         NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers),\n311: \t\tprocessor:                       processor,\n312: \t\tlisterWatcher:                   lw,\n313: \t\tobjectType:                      exampleObject,\n314: \t\tobjectDescription:               options.ObjectDescription,\n315: \t\tresyncCheckPeriod:               options.ResyncPeriod,\n316: \t\tdefaultEventHandlerResyncPeriod: options.ResyncPeriod,\n317: \t\tclock:                           realClock,\n318: \t\tcacheMutationDetector:           NewCacheMutationDetector(fmt.Sprintf(\"%T\", exampleObject)),\n319: \t\tkeyFunc:                         DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc,\n320: \t}\n321: }\n322: \n323: // SharedIndexInformerOptions configures a sharedIndexInformer.\n324: type SharedIndexInformerOptions struct {\n325: \t// ResyncPeriod is the default event handler resync period and resync check\n326: \t// period. This is useful for determining if caches have synced.\n338: type InformerSynced func() bool\n339: \n340: const (\n341: \t// syncedPollPeriod controls how often you look at the status of your sync funcs\n342: \tsyncedPollPeriod = 100 * time.Millisecond\n343: \n344: \t// initialBufferSize is the initial number of event notifications that can be buffered.\n345: \tinitialBufferSize = 1024\n346: )\n347: \n348: // WaitForNamedCacheSync is a wrapper around WaitForCacheSync that generates log messages\n349: // indicating that the caller identified by name is waiting for syncs, followed by\n350: // either a successful or failed sync.\n351: //\n352: // Contextual logging: WaitForNamedCacheSyncWithContext should be used instead of WaitForNamedCacheSync in code which supports contextual logging.\n353: func WaitForNamedCacheSync(controllerName string, stopCh <-chan struct{}, cacheSyncs ...InformerSynced) bool {\n354: \tklog.Background().Info(\"Waiting for caches to sync\", \"controller\", controllerName)\n355: \n356: \tif !WaitForCacheSync(stopCh, cacheSyncs...) {\n357: \t\tutilruntime.HandleErrorWithContext(context.Background(), nil, \"Unable to sync caches\", \"controller\", controllerName)\n358: \t\treturn false\n359: \t}\n360: \n361: \tklog.Background().Info(\"Caches are synced\", \"controller\", controllerName)\n362: \treturn true\n363: }\n364: \n365: // WaitForNamedCacheSyncWithContext is a wrapper around WaitForCacheSyncWithContext that generates log messages\n366: // indicating that the caller is waiting for syncs, followed by either a successful or failed sync.\n367: //\n368: // Contextual logging can be used to identify the caller in those log messages. It returns true if it was successful, false\n387: // if the controller should shutdown\n388: // callers should prefer WaitForNamedCacheSync()\n389: func WaitForCacheSync(stopCh <-chan struct{}, cacheSyncs ...InformerSynced) bool {\n390: \terr := wait.PollImmediateUntil(syncedPollPeriod,\n391: \t\tfunc() (bool, error) {\n392: \t\t\tfor _, syncFunc := range cacheSyncs {\n393: \t\t\t\tif !syncFunc() {\n394: \t\t\t\t\treturn false, nil\n395: \t\t\t\t}\n396: \t\t\t}\n397: \t\t\treturn true, nil\n398: \t\t},\n399: \t\tstopCh)\n400: \tif err != nil {\n401: \t\treturn false\n402: \t}\n403: \n404: \treturn true\n405: }\n406: \n407: // `*sharedIndexInformer` implements SharedIndexInformer and has three\n408: // main components.  One is an indexed local cache, `indexer Indexer`.\n409: // The second main component is a Controller that pulls\n410: // objects/notifications using the ListerWatcher and pushes them into\n411: // a DeltaFIFO --- whose knownObjects is the informer's local cache\n412: // --- while concurrently Popping Deltas values from that fifo and\n413: // processing them with `sharedIndexInformer::HandleDeltas`.  Each\n414: // invocation of HandleDeltas, which is done with the fifo's lock\n415: // held, processes each Delta in turn.  For each Delta this both\n416: // updates the local cache and stuffs the relevant notification into\n417: // the sharedProcessor.  The third main component is that\n418: // sharedProcessor, which is responsible for relaying those\n419: // notifications to each of the informer's clients.\n420: type sharedIndexInformer struct {\n421: \tindexer    Indexer\n422: \tcontroller Controller\n423: \n424: \tprocessor             *sharedProcessor\n425: \tcacheMutationDetector MutationDetector\n426: \n427: \tlisterWatcher ListerWatcher\n428: \n429: \t// objectType is an example object of the type this informer is expected to handle. There are two\n799: // kinds of distribute operations.  The sync distributions go to a\n800: // subset of the listeners that (a) is recomputed in the occasional\n801: // calls to shouldResync and (b) every listener is initially put in.\n802: // The non-sync distributions go to every listener.\n803: type sharedProcessor struct {\n804: \tlistenersStarted bool\n805: \tlistenersLock    sync.RWMutex\n806: \tlistenersRCond   *sync.Cond // Caller of Wait must hold a read lock on listenersLock.\n807: \t// Map from listeners to whether or not they are currently syncing\n808: \tlisteners map[*processorListener]bool\n809: \tclock     clock.Clock\n810: \twg        wait.Group\n811: }\n812: \n813: func (p *sharedProcessor) getListener(registration ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) *processorListener {\n814: \tp.listenersLock.RLock()\n815: \tdefer p.listenersLock.RUnlock()\n816: \n817: \tif p.listeners == nil {\n818: \t\treturn nil\n819: \t}\n820: \n821: \tif result, ok := registration.(*processorListener); ok {\n822: \t\tif _, exists := p.listeners[result]; exists {\n823: \t\t\treturn result\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t}\n826: \n827: \treturn nil\n828: }\n829: \n830: func (p *sharedProcessor) addListener(listener *processorListener) ResourceEventHandlerRegistration {\n831: \tp.listenersLock.Lock()\n832: \tdefer p.listenersLock.Unlock()\n833: \n834: \tif p.listeners == nil {\n835: \t\tp.listeners = make(map[*processorListener]bool)\n836: \t}\n837: \n838: \tp.listeners[listener] = true\n839: \n840: \tif p.listenersStarted {\n841: \t\tp.wg.Start(listener.run)\n842: \t\tp.wg.Start(listener.pop)\n843: \t}\n844: \n845: \treturn listener\n846: }\n847: \n848: func (p *sharedProcessor) removeListener(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error {\n849: \tp.listenersLock.Lock()\n850: \tdefer p.listenersLock.Unlock()\n851: \n852: \tlistener, ok := handle.(*processorListener)\n853: \tif !ok {\n854: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"invalid key type %t\", handle)\n855: \t} else if p.listeners == nil {\n856: \t\t// No listeners are registered, do nothing\n857: \t\treturn nil\n858: \t} else if _, exists := p.listeners[listener]; !exists {\n859: \t\t// Listener is not registered, just do nothing\n860: \t\treturn nil\n861: \t}\n862: \n863: \tdelete(p.listeners, listener)\n864: \n865: \tif p.listenersStarted {\n866: \t\tclose(listener.addCh)\n867: \t}\n868: \n869: \treturn nil\n870: }\n871: \n872: func (p *sharedProcessor) distribute(obj interface{}, sync bool) {\n873: \tp.listenersLock.RLock()\n874: \tdefer p.listenersLock.RUnlock()\n875: \n876: \t// Before we start blocking on writes to the listeners' channels,\n877: \t// ensure that they all have been started. If the processor stops,\n878: \t// p.listeners gets cleared, in which case we also continue here\n879: \t// and return without doing anything.\n880: \tfor !p.listenersStarted && len(p.listeners) > 0 {\n881: \t\tp.listenersRCond.Wait()\n882: \t}\n883: \n884: \tfor listener, isSyncing := range p.listeners {\n885: \t\tswitch {\n886: \t\tcase !sync:\n887: \t\t\t// non-sync messages are delivered to every listener\n888: \t\t\tlistener.add(obj)\n889: \t\tcase isSyncing:\n890: \t\t\t// sync messages are delivered to every syncing listener\n891: \t\t\tlistener.add(obj)\n892: \t\tdefault:\n893: \t\t\t// skipping a sync obj for a non-syncing listener\n894: \t\t}\n895: \t}\n896: }\n897: \n898: // sharedProcessorRunHook can be used inside tests to execute additional code\n899: // at the start of sharedProcessor.run.\n900: var sharedProcessorRunHook atomic.Pointer[func()]\n901: \n902: func (p *sharedProcessor) run(ctx context.Context) {\n903: \tfunc() {\n904: \t\thook := sharedProcessorRunHook.Load()\n905: \t\tif hook != nil {\n906: \t\t\t(*hook)()\n907: \t\t}\n908: \t\t// Changing listenersStarted needs a write lock.\n909: \t\tp.listenersLock.Lock()\n910: \t\tdefer p.listenersLock.Unlock()\n911: \t\tfor listener := range p.listeners {\n912: \t\t\tp.wg.Start(listener.run)\n913: \t\t\tp.wg.Start(listener.pop)\n914: \t\t}\n915: \t\tp.listenersStarted = true\n916: \t\tp.listenersRCond.Signal()\n917: \t}()\n918: \t<-ctx.Done()\n919: \n920: \tp.listenersLock.Lock()\n921: \tdefer p.listenersLock.Unlock()\n922: \tfor listener := range p.listeners {\n923: \t\tclose(listener.addCh) // Tell .pop() to stop. .pop() will tell .run() to stop\n924: \t}\n925: \n926: \t// Wipe out list of listeners since they are now closed\n927: \t// (processorListener cannot be re-used)\n928: \tp.listeners = nil\n929: \n930: \t// Reset to false since no listeners are running\n931: \tp.listenersStarted = false\n932: \n933: \t// Wake up sharedProcessor.distribute.\n934: \tp.listenersRCond.Signal()\n935: \n936: \tp.wg.Wait() // Wait for all .pop() and .run() to stop\n937: }\n938: \n939: // shouldResync queries every listener to determine if any of them need a resync, based on each\n940: // listener's resyncPeriod.\n941: func (p *sharedProcessor) shouldResync() bool {\n942: \tp.listenersLock.Lock()\n943: \tdefer p.listenersLock.Unlock()\n944: \n945: \tresyncNeeded := false\n946: \tnow := p.clock.Now()\n947: \tfor listener := range p.listeners {\n948: \t\t// need to loop through all the listeners to see if they need to resync so we can prepare any\n949: \t\t// listeners that are going to be resyncing.\n950: \t\tshouldResync := listener.shouldResync(now)\n951: \t\tp.listeners[listener] = shouldResync\n952: \n953: \t\tif shouldResync {\n954: \t\t\tresyncNeeded = true\n955: \t\t\tlistener.determineNextResync(now)\n956: \t\t}\n957: \t}\n958: \treturn resyncNeeded\n959: }\n960: \n961: func (p *sharedProcessor) resyncCheckPeriodChanged(logger klog.Logger, resyncCheckPeriod time.Duration) {\n962: \tp.listenersLock.RLock()\n963: \tdefer p.listenersLock.RUnlock()\n964: \n965: \tfor listener := range p.listeners {\n966: \t\tresyncPeriod := determineResyncPeriod(\n967: \t\t\tlogger, listener.requestedResyncPeriod, resyncCheckPeriod)\n968: \t\tlistener.setResyncPeriod(resyncPeriod)\n969: \t}\n970: }\n971: \n972: // processorListener relays notifications from a sharedProcessor to\n973: // one ResourceEventHandler --- using two goroutines, two unbuffered\n974: // channels, and an unbounded ring buffer.  The `add(notification)`\n975: // function sends the given notification to `addCh`.  One goroutine\n976: // runs `pop()`, which pumps notifications from `addCh` to `nextCh`\n977: // using storage in the ring buffer while `nextCh` is not keeping up.\n978: // Another goroutine runs `run()`, which receives notifications from\n979: // `nextCh` and synchronously invokes the appropriate handler method.\n980: //\n981: // processorListener also keeps track of the adjusted requested resync\n982: // period of the listener.\n983: type processorListener struct {\n984: \tlogger klog.Logger\n985: \tnextCh chan interface{}\n986: \taddCh  chan interface{}\n987: \n988: \thandler ResourceEventHandler\n989: \n990: \tsyncTracker *synctrack.SingleFileTracker\n991: \n992: \t// pendingNotifications is an unbounded ring buffer that holds all notifications not yet distributed.\n993: \t// There is one per listener, but a failing/stalled listener will have infinite pendingNotifications\n994: \t// added until we OOM.\n995: \t// TODO: This is no worse than before, since reflectors were backed by unbounded DeltaFIFOs, but\n996: \t// we should try to do something better.\n997: \tpendingNotifications buffer.RingGrowing\n998: \n999: \t// requestedResyncPeriod is how frequently the listener wants a\n1000: \t// full resync from the shared informer, but modified by two\n1001: \t// adjustments.  One is imposing a lower bound,\n1002: \t// `minimumResyncPeriod`.  The other is another lower bound, the\n1003: \t// sharedIndexInformer's `resyncCheckPeriod`, that is imposed (a) only\n1004: \t// in AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod invocations made after the\n1005: \t// sharedIndexInformer starts and (b) only if the informer does\n1006: \t// resyncs at all.\n1007: \trequestedResyncPeriod time.Duration\n1008: \t// resyncPeriod is the threshold that will be used in the logic\n1009: \t// for this listener.  This value differs from\n1010: \t// requestedResyncPeriod only when the sharedIndexInformer does\n1011: \t// not do resyncs, in which case the value here is zero. Because unicode.C\\n377: \\t// contains newline and tab characters that we want.\\n378: \\tallowedRanges := []*unicode.RangeTable{\\n379: \\t\\tunicode.L,\\n380: \\t\\tunicode.M,\\n381: \\t\\tunicode.N,\\n382: \\t\\tunicode.P,\\n383: \\t\\tunicode.S,\\n384: \\t\\tunicode.Z,\\n385: \\t\\t&spaceControlCharacters,\\n386: \\t}\\n387: \\tbuilder := strings.Builder{}\\n388: \\tfor _, roon := range s {\\n389: \\t\\tif unicode.IsOneOf(allowedRanges, roon) {\\n390: \\t\\t\\tbuilder.WriteRune(roon) // returns nil error, per go doc\\n391: \\t\\t} else {\\n392: \\t\\t\\tfmt.Fprintf(&builder, \\\"%U\\\", roon)\\n393: \\t\\t}\\n394: \\t}\\n395: \\treturn builder.String()\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // Namespace implements ClientConfig\\n399: func (config *DirectClientConfig) Namespace() (string, bool, error) {\\n400: \\tif config.overrides != nil && config.overrides.Context.Namespace != \\\"\\\" {\\n401: \\t\\t// In the event we have an empty config but we do have a namespace override, we should return\\n402: \\t\\t// the namespace override instead of having config.ConfirmUsable() return an error. }\n362: \n363: // cleanANSIEscapeCodes takes an arbitrary string and ensures that there are no\n364: // ANSI escape sequences that could put the terminal in a weird state (e.g.,\n365: // \"\\e[1m\" bolds text)\n366: func cleanANSIEscapeCodes(s string) string {\n367: \t// spaceControlCharacters includes tab, new line, vertical tab, new page, and\n368: \t// carriage return. These are in the unicode.Cc category, but that category also\n369: \t// contains ESC (U+001B) which we don't want.\n370: \tspaceControlCharacters := unicode.RangeTable{\n371: \t\tR16: []unicode.Range16{\n372: \t\t\t{Lo: 0x0009, Hi: 0x000D, Stride: 1},\n373: \t\t},\n374: \t}\n375: \n376: \t// Why not make this deny-only (instead of allow-only)? Because unicode.C\n377: \t// contains newline and tab characters that we want.\n378: \tallowedRanges := []*unicode.RangeTable{\n379: \t\tunicode.L,\n380: \t\tunicode.M,\n381: \t\tunicode.N,\n382: \t\tunicode.P,\n383: \t\tunicode.S,\n384: \t\tunicode.Z,\n385: \t\t&spaceControlCharacters,\n386: \t}\n387: \tbuilder := strings.Builder{}\n388: \tfor _, roon := range s {\n389: \t\tif unicode.IsOneOf(allowedRanges, roon) {\n390: \t\t\tbuilder.WriteRune(roon) // returns nil error, per go doc\n391: \t\t} else {\n392: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&builder, \"%U\", roon)\n393: \t\t}\n394: \t}\n395: \treturn builder.String()\n396: }\n397: \n398: // Namespace implements ClientConfig\n399: func (config *DirectClientConfig) Namespace() (string, bool, error) {\n400: \tif config.overrides != nil && config.overrides.Context.Namespace != \"\" {\n401: \t\t// In the event we have an empty config but we do have a namespace override, we should return\n402: \t\t// the namespace override instead of having config.ConfirmUsable() return an error. Each Apply function takes an \\\"apply\\n25: configuration\\\" type as an argument, which is a structured representation of an Apply request. For\\n26: example:\\n27: \\n28: \\timport (\\n29: \\t     ...\\n30: \\t     v1ac \\\"k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/autoscaling/v1\\\"\\n31: \\t)\\n32: \\thpaApplyConfig := v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscaler(autoscalerName, ns).\\n33: \\t     WithSpec(v1ac.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec().\\n34: \\t              WithMinReplicas(0)\\n35: \\t     )\\n36: \\treturn hpav1client.Apply(ctx, hpaApplyConfig, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \\\"mycontroller\\\", Force: true})\\n37: \\n38: Note in this example that HorizontalPodAutoscaler is imported from an \\\"applyconfigurations\\\"\\n39: package. Each \\\"apply configuration\\\" type represents the same Kubernetes object kind as the\\n40: corresponding go struct, but where all fields are pointers to make them optional, allowing apply\\n41: requests to be accurately represented. For example, this when the apply configuration in the above\\n42: example is marshalled to YAML, it produces:\\n43: \\n44: \\tapiVersion: autoscaling/v1\\n45: \\tkind: HorizontalPodAutoscaler\\n46: \\tmetadata:\\n47: \\t    name: myHPA\\n48: \\t    namespace: myNamespace\\n49: \\tspec:\\n50: \\t    minReplicas: 0\\n51: \\n52: To understand why this is needed, the above YAML cannot be produced by the\\n53: v1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler go struct. Take for example:\\n54: \\n55: \\thpa := v1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler{\\n56: \\t     TypeMeta: metav1.TypeMeta{\\n57: \\t              APIVersion: \\\"autoscaling/v1\\\",\\n58: \\t              Kind:       \\\"HorizontalPodAutoscaler\\\",\\n59: \\t     },\\n60: \\t     ObjectMeta: ObjectMeta{\\n61: \\t              Namespace: ns,\\n62: \\t              Name:      autoscalerName,\\n63: \\t     },\\n64: \\t     Spec: v1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec{\\n65: \\t              MinReplicas: pointer.Int32Ptr(0),\\n66: \\t     },\\n67: \\t}\\n68: \\n69: The above code attempts to declare the same apply configuration as shown in the previous examples,\\n70: but when marshalled to YAML, produces:\\n71: \\n72: \\tkind: HorizontalPodAutoscaler\\n73: \\tapiVersion: autoscaling/v1\\n74: \\tmetadata:\\n75: \\t  name: myHPA\\n76: \\t  namespace: myNamespace\\n77: \\tspec:\\n78: \\t  scaleTargetRef:\\n79: \\t    kind: \\\"\\\"\\n80: \\t    name: \\\"\\\"\\n81: \\t  minReplicas: 0\\n82: \\t  maxReplicas: 0\\n83: \\n84: Which, among other things, contains spec.maxReplicas set to 0. This is almost certainly not what\\n85: the caller intended (the intended apply configuration says nothing about the maxReplicas field),\\n86: and could have serious consequences on a production system: it directs the autoscaler to downscale\\n87: to zero pods. The problem here originates from the fact that the go structs contain required fields\\n88: that are zero valued if not set explicitly. The go structs work as intended for create and update\\n89: operations, but are fundamentally incompatible with apply, which is why we have introduced the\\n90: generated \\\"apply configuration\\\" types.\\n91: \\n92: The \\\"apply configurations\\\" also have convenience With<FieldName> functions that make it easier to\\n93: build apply requests. This allows developers to set fields without having to deal with the fact that\\n94: all the fields in the \\\"apply configuration\\\" types are pointers, and are inconvenient to set using\\n95: go. For example \\\"MinReplicas: &0\\\" is not legal go code, so without the With functions, developers\\n96: would work around this problem by using a library, .e.g. \\\"MinReplicas: pointer.Int32Ptr(0)\\\", but\\n97: string enumerations like corev1.Protocol are still a problem since they cannot be supported by a\\n98: general purpose library. In addition to the convenience, the With functions also isolate\\n99: developers from the underlying representation, which makes it safer for the underlying\\n100: representation to be changed to support additional features in the future.\\n101: \\n102: # Controller Support\\n103: \\n104: The new client-go support makes it much easier to use Server-side Apply in controllers, by either of\\n105: two mechanisms.\\n106: \\n107: Mechanism 1:\\n108: \\n109: When authoring new controllers to use Server-side Apply, a good approach is to have the controller\\n110: recreate the apply configuration for an object each time it reconciles that object.  This ensures\\n111: that the controller fully reconciles all the fields that it is responsible for. Controllers\\n112: typically should unconditionally set all the fields they own by setting \\\"Force: true\\\" in the\\n113: ApplyOptions. Controllers must also provide a FieldManager name that is unique to the\\n114: reconciliation loop that apply is called from.\\n115: \\n116: When upgrading existing controllers to use Server-side Apply the same approach often works\\n117: well--migrate the controllers to recreate the apply configuration each time it reconciles any\\n118: object. For cases where this does not work well, see Mechanism 2.\\n119: \\n120: Mechanism 2:\\n121: \\n122: When upgrading existing controllers to use Server-side Apply, the controller might have multiple\\n123: code paths that update different parts of an object depending on various conditions. Migrating a\\n124: controller like this to Server-side Apply can be risky because if the controller forgets to include\\n125: any fields in an apply configuration that is included in a previous apply request, a field can be\\n126: accidentally deleted. For such cases, an alternative to mechanism 1 is to replace any controller\\n127: reconciliation code that performs a \\\"read/modify-in-place/update\\\" (or patch) workflow with a\\n128: \\\"extract/modify-in-place/apply\\\" workflow. Here's an example of the new workflow:\\n129: \\n130: \\t    fieldMgr := \\\"my-field-manager\\\"\\n131: \\t    deploymentClient := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\\\"default\\\")\\n132: \\t    // read, could also be read from a shared informer\\n133: \\t    deployment, err := deploymentClient.Get(ctx, \\\"example-deployment\\\", metav1.GetOptions{})\\n134: \\t    if err != nil {\\n135: \\t      // handle error\\n136: \\t    }\\n137: \\t    // extract\\n138: \\t    deploymentApplyConfig, err := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)\\n139: \\t    if err != nil {\\n140: \\t      // handle error\\n141: \\t    }\\n142: \\t    // modify-in-place\\n143: \\t    deploymentApplyConfig.Spec.Template.Spec.WithContainers(corev1ac.Container().\\n144: \\t\\tWithName(\\\"modify-slice\\\").\\n145: \\t\\tWithImage(\\\"nginx:1.14.2\\\"),\\n146: \\t    )\\n147: \\t    // apply\\n148: \\t    applied, err := deploymentClient.Apply(ctx, extractedDeployment, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: fieldMgr})\\n149: */\\n150: package applyconfigurations\\n151: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go\"}",

Each \"apply configuration\" type represents the same Kubernetes object kind as the\n40: corresponding go struct, but where all fields are pointers to make them optional, allowing apply\n41: requests to be accurately represented. For example, this when the apply configuration in the above\n42: example is marshalled to YAML, it produces:\n43: \n44: \tapiVersion: autoscaling/v1\n45: \tkind: HorizontalPodAutoscaler\n46: \tmetadata:\n47: \t    name: myHPA\n48: \t    namespace: myNamespace\n49: \tspec:\n50: \t    minReplicas: 0\n51: \n52: To understand why this is needed, the above YAML cannot be produced by the\n53: v1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler go struct. Take for example:\n54: \n55: \thpa := v1.HorizontalPodAutoscaler{\n56: \t     TypeMeta: metav1.TypeMeta{\n57: \t              APIVersion: \"autoscaling/v1\",\n58: \t              Kind:       \"HorizontalPodAutoscaler\",\n59: \t     },\n60: \t     ObjectMeta: ObjectMeta{\n61: \t              Namespace: ns,\n62: \t              Name:      autoscalerName,\n63: \t     },\n64: \t     Spec: v1.HorizontalPodAutoscalerSpec{\n65: \t              MinReplicas: pointer.Int32Ptr(0),\n66: \t     },\n67: \t}\n68: \n69: The above code attempts to declare the same apply configuration as shown in the previous examples,\n70: but when marshalled to YAML, produces:\n71: \n72: \tkind: HorizontalPodAutoscaler\n73: \tapiVersion: autoscaling/v1\n74: \tmetadata:\n75: \t  name: myHPA\n76: \t  namespace: myNamespace\n77: \tspec:\n78: \t  scaleTargetRef:\n79: \t    kind: \"\"\n80: \t    name: \"\"\n81: \t  minReplicas: 0\n82: \t  maxReplicas: 0\n83: \n84: Which, among other things, contains spec.maxReplicas set to 0. This is almost certainly not what\n85: the caller intended (the intended apply configuration says nothing about the maxReplicas field),\n86: and could have serious consequences on a production system: it directs the autoscaler to downscale\n87: to zero pods. The problem here originates from the fact that the go structs contain required fields\n88: that are zero valued if not set explicitly. The go structs work as intended for create and update\n89: operations, but are fundamentally incompatible with apply, which is why we have introduced the\n90: generated \"apply configuration\" types.\n91: \n92: The \"apply configurations\" also have convenience With<FieldName> functions that make it easier to\n93: build apply requests. This allows developers to set fields without having to deal with the fact that\n94: all the fields in the \"apply configuration\" types are pointers, and are inconvenient to set using\n95: go. For example \"MinReplicas: &0\" is not legal go code, so without the With functions, developers\n96: would work around this problem by using a library, .e.g. \"MinReplicas: pointer.Int32Ptr(0)\", but\n97: string enumerations like corev1.Protocol are still a problem since they cannot be supported by a\n98: general purpose library. In addition to the convenience, the With functions also isolate\n99: developers from the underlying representation, which makes it safer for the underlying\n100: representation to be changed to support additional features in the future.\n101: \n102: # Controller Support\n103: \n104: The new client-go support makes it much easier to use Server-side Apply in controllers, by either of\n105: two mechanisms.\n106: \n107: Mechanism 1:\n108: \n109: When authoring new controllers to use Server-side Apply, a good approach is to have the controller\n110: recreate the apply configuration for an object each time it reconciles that object.  This ensures\n111: that the controller fully reconciles all the fields that it is responsible for. Controllers\n112: typically should unconditionally set all the fields they own by setting \"Force: true\" in the\n113: ApplyOptions. Controllers must also provide a FieldManager name that is unique to the\n114: reconciliation loop that apply is called from.\n115: \n116: When upgrading existing controllers to use Server-side Apply the same approach often works\n117: well--migrate the controllers to recreate the apply configuration each time it reconciles any\n118: object. For cases where this does not work well, see Mechanism 2.\n119: \n120: Mechanism 2:\n121: \n122: When upgrading existing controllers to use Server-side Apply, the controller might have multiple\n123: code paths that update different parts of an object depending on various conditions. Migrating a\n124: controller like this to Server-side Apply can be risky because if the controller forgets to include\n125: any fields in an apply configuration that is included in a previous apply request, a field can be\n126: accidentally deleted. For such cases, an alternative to mechanism 1 is to replace any controller\n127: reconciliation code that performs a \"read/modify-in-place/update\" (or patch) workflow with a\n128: \"extract/modify-in-place/apply\" workflow. Here's an example of the new workflow:\n129: \n130: \t    fieldMgr := \"my-field-manager\"\n131: \t    deploymentClient := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\")\n132: \t    // read, could also be read from a shared informer\n133: \t    deployment, err := deploymentClient.Get(ctx, \"example-deployment\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n134: \t    if err != nil {\n135: \t      // handle error\n136: \t    }\n137: \t    // extract\n138: \t    deploymentApplyConfig, err := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldMgr)\n139: \t    if err != nil {\n140: \t      // handle error\n141: \t    }\n142: \t    // modify-in-place\n143: \t    deploymentApplyConfig.Spec.Template.Spec.WithContainers(corev1ac.Container().\n144: \t\tWithName(\"modify-slice\").\n145: \t\tWithImage(\"nginx:1.14.2\"),\n146: \t    )\n147: \t    // apply\n148: \t    applied, err := deploymentClient.Apply(ctx, extractedDeployment, metav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: fieldMgr})\n149: */\n150: package applyconfigurations\n151: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/doc.go"

This policy applies to\n135: every version greater than or equal to 2.0.\n136: \n137: #### Why do the 1.4 and 1.5 branch contain top-level folder named after the version?\n138: \n139: For the initial release of client-go, we thought it would be easiest to keep\n140: separate directories for each minor version. That soon proved to be a mistake.\n141: We are keeping the top-level folders in the 1.4 and 1.5 branches so that\n142: existing users won't be broken.\n143: \n144: ### Kubernetes tags\n145: \n146: This repository is still a mirror of\n147: [k8s.io/kubernetes/staging/src/client-go](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/tree/master/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go),\n148: the code development is still done in the staging area.\n149: \n150: Since Kubernetes `v1.8.0`, when syncing the code from the staging area,\n151: we also sync the Kubernetes version tags to client-go, prefixed with\n152: `kubernetes-`. From Kubernetes `v1.17.0`, we also create matching semver\n153: `v0.x.y` tags for each `v1.x.y` Kubernetes release.\n154: \n155: For example, if you check out the `kubernetes-1.17.0` or the `v0.17.0` tag in\n156: client-go, the code you get is exactly the same as if you check out the `v1.17.0`\n157: tag in Kubernetes, and change directory to `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go`.\n158: \n159: The purpose is to let users quickly find matching commits among published repos,\n160: like [sample-apiserver](https://github.com/kubernetes/sample-apiserver),\n161: [apiextension-apiserver](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiextensions-apiserver),\n162: etc. The Kubernetes version tag does NOT claim any backwards compatibility\n163: guarantees for client-go. Please check the [semantic versions](#versioning) if\n164: you care about backwards compatibility.\n165: \n166: ### How to get it\n167: \n168: To get the latest version, use go1.16+ and fetch using the `go get` command. For example:\n169: \n170: ```\n171: go get k8s.io/client-go@latest\n172: ```\n173: \n174: To get a specific version, use go1.11+ and fetch the desired version using the `go get` command. For example:\n175: \n176: ```\n177: go get k8s.io/client-go@v0.20.4\n178: ```\n179: \n180: See [INSTALL.md](/INSTALL.md) for detailed instructions and troubleshooting.\n181: \n182: ### How to use it\n183: \n184: If your application runs in a Pod in the cluster, please refer to the\n185: in-cluster [example](examples/in-cluster-client-configuration), otherwise please\n186: refer to the out-of-cluster [example](examples/out-of-cluster-client-configuration).\n187: \n188: ### Dependency management\n189: \n190: For details on how to correctly use a dependency management for installing client-go, please see [INSTALL.md](INSTALL.md).\n191: \n192: ### Contributing code\n193: Please send pull requests against the client packages in the Kubernetes main [repository](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes). Changes in the staging area will be published to this repository every day.\n194: ",

  "content": "/*\nCopyright 2024 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\n/*\nPackage clientgo is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API.\nIt provides programmatic access to the Kubernetes API server, enabling\napplications to create, read, update, and delete Kubernetes resources,\nas well as watch for changes and build controllers.\n\n# Key Packages\n\nThe client-go library is organized into several sub-packages, each serving\na specific purpose:\n\n## kubernetes\n\nThe kubernetes package (k8s.io/client-go/kubernetes) provides a typed\nClientset for accessing the Kubernetes API. The Clientset contains clients\nfor each API group/version and provides compile-time type safety. Use this\nfor interacting with built-in Kubernetes resources:\n\n\tclientset, err := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\n\tpods, err := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").List(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})\n\tdeployment, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"myapp\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n\n## dynamic\n\nThe dynamic package (k8s.io/client-go/dynamic) provides a client that can\nwork with arbitrary Kubernetes resources without compile-time type information.\nThis is essential for working with Custom Resource Definitions (CRDs) or when\nthe resource type is not known at compile time:\n\n\tdynamicClient, err := dynamic.NewForConfig(config)\n\tgvr := schema.GroupVersionResource{Group: \"example.com\", Version: \"v1\", Resource: \"myresources\"}\n\tunstructuredObj, err := dynamicClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"myresource\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n\n## discovery\n\nThe discovery package (k8s.io/client-go/discovery) provides clients for\ndiscovering the API groups, versions, and resources supported by a Kubernetes\nAPI server. This is useful for determining capabilities at runtime:\n\n\tdiscoveryClient, err := discovery.NewDiscoveryClientForConfig(config)\n\tgroups, resources, err := discoveryClient.ServerGroupsAndResources()\n\n## rest\n\nThe rest package (k8s.io/client-go/rest) provides lower-level REST client\nfunctionality and configuration. It includes the Config type which holds\nconnection parameters and is used to initialize all higher-level clients:\n\n\tconfig := &rest.Config{\n\t\tHost:        \"https://kubernetes.default.svc\",\n\t\tBearerToken: token,\n\t\tTLSClientConfig: rest.TLSClientConfig{\n\t\t\tCAFile: \"/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt\",\n\t\t},\n\t}\n\n## tools/cache\n\nThe tools/cache package (k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache) provides the\nfoundational components for building controllers: Informers, Listers,\nand Indexers. SharedInformers efficiently watch resources and maintain\na local cache, while Listers provide read access to that cache:\n\n\tinformer := cache.NewSharedIndexInformer(\n\t\t&cache.ListWatch{...},\n\t\t&v1.Pod{},\n\t\tresyncPeriod,\n\t\tcache.Indexers{cache.NamespaceIndex: cache.MetaNamespaceIndexFunc},\n\t)\n\tinformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n\t\tAddFunc:    onAdd,\n\t\tUpdateFunc: onUpdate,\n\t\tDeleteFunc: onDelete,\n\t})\n\n## tools/clientcmd\n\nThe tools/clientcmd package (k8s.io/client-go/tools/clientcmd) provides\nutilities for loading kubeconfig files and building client configurations.\nIt handles the complexity of multiple contexts, clusters, and authentication\nmethods found in kubeconfig files:\n\n\tconfig, err := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(\"\", kubeconfigPath)\n\t// Or using the default loading rules:\n\tconfig, err := clientcmd.NewNonInteractiveDeferredLoadingClientConfig(\n\t\tclientcmd.NewDefaultClientConfigLoadingRules(),\n\t\t&clientcmd.ConfigOverrides{},\n\t).ClientConfig()\n\n## informers\n\nThe informers package (k8s.io/client-go/informers) provides a SharedInformerFactory\nthat creates and manages SharedInformers for all built-in Kubernetes types.\nThis is the recommended way to watch resources in controllers:\n\n\tfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, resyncPeriod)\n\tpodInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\n\tpodLister := podInformer.Lister()\n\tfactory.Start(stopCh)\n\n## applyconfigurations\n\nThe applyconfigurations package (k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations) provides\ntypesafe Go representations for Server-Side Apply requests. These types have\nall fields as pointers, enabling precise control over which fields are set\nin apply operations.\n\n# Connecting to the API Server\n\n## In-Cluster Configuration\n\nWhen running inside a Kubernetes cluster (e.g., in a Pod), use InClusterConfig\nwhich reads credentials from the service account mounted into the pod:\n\n\tconfig, err := rest.InClusterConfig()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\t// handle error\n\t}\n\tclientset, err := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\n\n## Out-of-Cluster Configuration\n\nWhen running outside a cluster, load configuration from a kubeconfig file:\n\n\tconfig, err := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(\"\", filepath.Join(homedir.HomeDir(), \".kube\", \"config\"))\n\t// Or use the KUBECONFIG environment variable:\n\tconfig, err := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(\"\", os.Getenv(\"KUBECONFIG\"))\n\n# Interacting with API Objects\n\n## Typed Clients\n\nFor built-in Kubernetes resources, use the typed clients from the kubernetes\npackage. These provide compile-time type safety and IDE support:\n\n\t// Create a Deployment\n\tdeployment := &appsv1.Deployment{...}\n\tresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Create(ctx, deployment, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n\n\t// Update a ConfigMap\n\tconfigMap.Data[\"key\"] = \"new-value\"\n\tresult, err := clientset.CoreV1().ConfigMaps(\"default\").Update(ctx, configMap, metav1.UpdateOptions{})\n\n## Dynamic Clients\n\nFor Custom Resources or when types are not known at compile time, use the\ndynamic client with unstructured.Unstructured objects:\n\n\tgvr := schema.GroupVersionResource{Group: \"stable.example.com\", Version: \"v1\", Resource: \"crontabs\"}\n\tcrontab := &unstructured.Unstructured{\n\t\tObject: map[string]interface{}{\n\t\t\t\"apiVersion\": \"stable.example.com/v1\",\n\t\t\t\"kind\":       \"CronTab\",\n\t\t\t\"metadata\":   map[string]interface{}{\"name\": \"my-crontab\"},\n\t\t\t\"spec\":       map[string]interface{}{\"cronSpec\": \"* * * * *\"},\n\t\t},\n\t}\n\tresult, err := dynamicClient.Resource(gvr).Namespace(\"default\").Create(ctx, crontab, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n\n## Server-Side Apply\n\nServer-Side Apply provides declarative configuration management with field\nownership tracking. Use the Apply methods with applyconfigurations types:\n\n\tdeploymentApply := appsv1ac.Deployment(\"my-deployment\", \"default\").\n\t\tWithSpec(appsv1ac.DeploymentSpec().\n\t\t\tWithReplicas(3).\n\t\t\tWithSelector(metav1ac.LabelSelector().\n\t\t\t\tWithMatchLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"myapp\"})))\n\tresult, err := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Apply(\n\t\tctx,\n\t\tdeploymentApply,\n\t\tmetav1.ApplyOptions{FieldManager: \"my-controller\"},\n\t)\n\n# Building Controllers\n\nControllers are the primary pattern for extending Kubernetes. They watch\nresources and reconcile actual state with desired state. The controller\npattern involves several components from client-go:\n\n## SharedInformers and Listers\n\nSharedInformers watch the API server and maintain a local cache of objects.\nListers provide read access to this cache without hitting the API server:\n\n\tfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, time.Hour)\n\tdeploymentInformer := factory.Apps().V1().Deployments()\n\tdeploymentLister := deploymentInformer.Lister()\n\n\t// Read from cache\n\tdeployment, err := deploymentLister.Deployments(\"default\").Get(\"my-deployment\")\n\n## Workqueues\n\nThe tools/workqueue package (k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue) provides\nrate-limited workqueues for decoupling event handling from processing:\n\n\tqueue := workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue(workqueue.DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter[string]())\n\tinformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n\t\tAddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n\t\t\tkey, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n\t\t\tqueue.Add(key)\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\n## Leader Election\n\nThe tools/leaderelection package (k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection)\nprovides leader election for high-availability controllers. Only the leader\nperforms reconciliation while followers remain on standby:\n\n\tlock := &resourcelock.LeaseLock{...}\n\tleaderelection.RunOrDie(ctx, leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{\n\t\tLock:          lock,\n\t\tLeaseDuration: 15 * time.Second,\n\t\tRenewDeadline: 10 * time.Second,\n\t\tRetryPeriod:   2 * time.Second,\n\t\tCallbacks: leaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{\n\t\t\tOnStartedLeading: func(ctx context.Context) { runController(ctx) },\n\t\t\tOnStoppedLeading: func() { os.Exit(0) },\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\n## WaitForCacheSync\n\nBefore processing events, controllers must wait for informer caches to sync\nwith the API server:\n\n\tfactory.Start(stopCh)\n\tif !cache.WaitForCacheSync(stopCh, deploymentInformer.Informer().HasSynced) {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to sync caches\")\n\t}\n*/\npackage clientgo\n",

The Clientset contains clients\nfor each API group/version and provides compile-time type safety.
